✦ SYSTEM DISCOVERY REPORT: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Status: FINAL (System Discovery Complete)

  ---

  BUSINESS PURPOSE

  Product Overview
  SpendOS is an enterprise-grade financial operations platform designed for high-integrity expense management. It prioritizes financial correctness through
  a ledger-first architecture, ensuring that every business event is backed by a double-entry accounting record.

  Problem Solved
   - Trust Gap: Traditional expense tools often lack a verifiable audit trail that matches actual money movement.
   - Approval Chaos: High-growth companies struggle with role-based visibility and strict state machine transitions for expenses.
   - Financial Integrity: Prevents "ghost" transactions or unbalanced books by enforcing Debits == Credits at the database level.

  User Personas
   1. Black Card (Owner/Founder): Full authority, manages company-wide settings and role creation.
   2. Admin (Operations Lead): Manages teams, freezes accounts, and overrides settings.
   3. Manager (Finance/Senior Ops): Approves expenses and manages the review queue.
   4. Employee (User): Submits expenses and raises tickets for payment delays.

  ---

  TECH STACK

  ┌──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Layer                │ Technology                                       │
  ├──────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Frontend             │ Next.js 15 (App Router), TypeScript, Vanilla CSS │
  │ Backend              │ Fastify (Node.js), TypeScript                    │
  │ Database             │ PostgreSQL (Neon), Prisma ORM                    │
  │ Ledger Engine        │ Custom Double-Entry Core (@spendos/ledger)       │
  │ Authentication       │ JWT (Access/Refresh Tokens), @spendos/auth       │
  │ Caching              │ Redis (Rate limiting, Pulse cache)               │
  │ Cloud/Infrastructure │ AWS S3 (Documents), Resend (Email), Docker       │
  │ Background Jobs      │ Node-cron (SLA), Outbox Processor (Reliability)  │
  └──────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  SYSTEM COMPONENTS

  1. Component Inventory

  │ Database     │ packages/database     │ Prisma schema and generated client for PostgreSQL.                       │

   15        │     └─► INSERT JournalEntry (CREDIT: Corporate Treasury)

   19                │
   20                ▼
   21 [OutboxProcessor] ───► [NotificationsService] ───► [User Dashboard]

  ---

  MODULE EXPLANATIONS

  Core Engine: @spendos/ledger
   - Purpose: Ensures transactional integrity for all financial movements.
   - Inputs: Account IDs, Transaction Type, Amount (Paise), Actor ID.
   - Outputs: Balanced JournalGroup and JournalEntries.
   - Dependencies: @spendos/database (Prisma).

  Lifecycle Service: ExpensesService
   - Purpose: Orchestrates the complex expense state machine.
   - Inputs: Submitter Actor, Amount, Category, Proof Documents.
   - Outputs: Expense record, Audit logs, Outbox events.
   - Dependencies: Ledger, PolicyEngine, S3, Notifications.

  Reliability Service: OutboxProcessor
   - Purpose: Guarantees that side effects (Emails, Notifications) occur exactly once, even if the API crashes.
   - Inputs: Pending OutboxEvent records.
   - Outputs: Outgoing emails, in-app notifications.
   - Dependencies: Prisma (FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED), EmailService.

  ---

  CODE HYGIENE & TECHNICAL DEBT

  Dead Code / Unused Services
   - OcrService (ocr.service.ts): Implemented using Tesseract.js but currently orphaned. It has a standalone route (POST /expenses/ocr) but is not
     integrated into the standard expense submission workflow.

  Incomplete Features
   - cleanupStaleLocks (cron.ts): Currently a placeholder. The system supports "review locks" (pessimistic locking in UI) but lacks the automatic cleanup
     for abandoned sessions.
   - Soft-Lock Schema: While server.ts checks for review_locked_by, the schema in schema.prisma has some fields but the logic for expiring them is not yet
     fully production-hardened.

  Experimental Code
   - antigravity-plugin/: Contains "Agents" and "Skills" markdown files. This appears to be a meta-layer for AI-assisted development or automated
     governance, rather than runtime application code.

  ---

  NEXT STEPS: System discovery is complete. The system is well-structured, follow-on tasks should focus on integrating the OCR service or completing the
  stale lock cleanup logic.

✦ SENIOR ARCHITECT REVIEW: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
  SpendOS has a strong foundation with its Ledger-First approach and Outbox Pattern. However, the implementation suffers from significant coupling between
  business logic and infrastructure, and several P0 scalability and reliability bottlenecks that will manifest under moderate load.

  ---

  2. ARCHITECTURAL FINDINGS

  [P0] Critical Vulnerabilities & Bottlenecks

  F1: Outbox Pattern "Processor-per-Instance" Conflict
   - Issue: The startOutboxWorker in server.ts runs a setInterval loop in every API pod. While it uses FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED, there is no coordination for
     event processing that has side effects (like sending emails via Resend).
   - Risk: Race conditions and duplicate external side effects (double emails) if the database doesn't lock fast enough across distributed nodes.
   - Fix: Extract the Outbox Processor into a standalone worker service or use a dedicated queue (Redis/BullMQ) to ensure single-responsibility processing.

  F2: Synchronous External Dependencies in Auth Flow
   - Issue: AuthService.register performs a ledger bootstrap and a database write, but other services (like UsersService.inviteUser) call sendEmail
     synchronously.
   - Risk: If the email provider (Resend) is slow or down, the user's request hangs, potentially timing out the database transaction.
   - Fix: Move all external side effects (Email, Slack, SMS) to the Outbox Pattern. Services should only write to OutboxEvent.

  F3: BigInt Serialization Overhead
   - Issue: The global setReplySerializer in server.ts uses a recursive JSON.stringify with a replacer for BigInt.
   - Risk: Extreme CPU overhead and latency for large responses (e.g., listing 100 journal entries), as it essentially double-serializes every response.
   - Fix: Use a custom JSON stringifier that handles BigInt natively or transform BigInt to string at the Service/DTO layer before serialization.

  ---

  [P1] Structural Design & Coupling

  F4: Service-to-Service Circular Coupling
   - Issue: ExpensesService depends on NotificationsService, and NotificationsService often references Expenses. There is no clear event-driven boundary.
   - Risk: Difficult to unit test in isolation and prone to circular dependency errors as the system grows.
   - Fix: Implement an Internal Event Bus. ExpensesService should emit an event; NotificationsService should listen.

  F5: Missing Aggregate Roots (Data Ownership)
   - Issue: The Ledger package is used directly by AuthService (for bootstrap) and ExpensesService (for payout). Business logic for "Account Creation" is
     scattered.
   - Risk: Violation of Data Ownership. If the ledger schema changes, multiple unrelated services break.
   - Fix: Create a FinancialOrchestrator that owns the relationship between "Business Entities" (Companies/Users) and "Financial Entities" (Accounts).

  ---

  [P2] Scalability & Efficiency

  F6: Audit Logging "Fire and Forget" Anti-pattern
   - Issue: AuditService.log uses an async call without await in many places (fire-and-forget).
   - Risk: Under high load, the Node.js event loop will be flooded with un-awaited promises. If the process crashes, audit logs are lost (Security Breach).
   - Fix: Audit logs are critical for compliance. They must be part of the ACID transaction or written to a reliable log-buffer (like Kafka or a local Redis
     stream).

  F7: Redis "Pulse" Cache Invalidation
   - Issue: activity.service.ts caches the "Dashboard Pulse" for 300s but invalidates it manually in ExpensesService.approveExpense.
   - Risk: Manual invalidation is fragile. Adding a new status or action will lead to stale dashboards.
   - Fix: Use Key Versioning or event-driven invalidation via the Outbox worker.

  ---

  3. CLASSIFIED REMEDIATION PLAN

  ┌────┬───────┬───────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ ID │ Class │ Title             │ Recommended Action                                          │
  ├────┼───────┼───────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ F1 │ P0    │ Outbox Scaling    │ Separate apps/worker from apps/api. Use BullMQ.             │
  │ F2 │ P0    │ Sync Side-Effects │ Audit all services; move sendEmail to Outbox.               │
  │ F3 │ P0    │ BigInt Perf       │ Implement bigint-json-serialization package.                │
  │ F4 │ P1    │ Circular Deps     │ Introduce EventEmitter2 or similar for cross-service comms. │
  │ F5 │ P1    │ Ledger Boundary   │ Move account seeding to LedgerService factory.              │
  │ F6 │ P2    │ Audit Integrity   │ Wrap AuditLog in the primary Prisma transaction.            │
  └────┴───────┴───────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ARCHITECTURAL SCORECARD

   - Separation of Concerns: B- (Business logic is leaking into controllers).
   - Coupling: C (High coupling between Domain and Infrastructure).
   - Cohesion: A- (Ledger logic is very cohesive).
   - API Design: B+ (Good use of Zod and Fastify Type Providers).
   - Scalability: C- (Outbox and BigInt issues will cause early failure).

  ---

  FINAL VERDICT: The "Ledger-First" strategy is a winner. The "Outbox" implementation is the weakest link. Fix F1 and F2 immediately to ensure production
  readiness.

  Security Architecture: Threat Modeling: Acting as a Security Architect to create a comprehensive threat model for the SpendOS application.


✦ SECURITY ARCHITECTURE REVIEW & THREAT MODEL

  Author: Security Architect
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target: SpendOS (Expense Reimbursement Engine & Ledger)

  ---

  1. ASSETS & TRUST BOUNDARIES

  1.1 Critical Assets
   1. The Ledger (System of Truth): JournalGroups and JournalEntries. Modification outside business rules equates to financial loss.
   2. Corporate Funds: Bank accounts linked to the Nodal Payout Account.
   3. PII & Identity Data: User emails, GSTINs, full names, password hashes.
   4. Expense Proof (Receipts): S3 Buckets containing potentially sensitive corporate spending data.
   5. Audit Logs: Irrefutable record of who did what.

  1.2 Trust Boundaries
   - TB-1: Internet ↔ Web Dashboard / Mobile: Untrusted client communicating with trusted frontend layer.
   - TB-2: Client ↔ API Gateway (Fastify): Untrusted payload entering the validation/auth boundary.
   - TB-3: API ↔ Database (Postgres): Trusted application executing logic against the persistence layer.
   - TB-4: API ↔ AWS S3: Direct client upload via pre-signed URLs (Semi-trusted interaction).
   - TB-5: Tenant ↔ Tenant: Strict logical boundary between company_A and company_B.

  ---

  2. ENTRY POINTS & ATTACK SURFACES

  2.1 Attack Surfaces
   1. Authentication & Session Management: /api/v1/auth/*
   2. Expense State Machine: /api/v1/expenses/:id/* (Approve, Reject, Mark Paid)
   3. File Uploads: S3 Pre-signed URL generation and confirmation.
   4. Role-Based Access Control (RBAC): API endpoint guards.
   5. Cross-Tenant Data Access (IDOR): Direct object references in APIs.

  2.2 Entry Points
   - Public API Routes (/login, /register, /invite).
   - Authenticated API Routes (Mutations like POST /expenses).
   - Direct S3 Upload endpoints.

  ---

  3. DATA FLOW THREAT MODEL (STRIDE)

  ┌──────────────┬────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Threat       │ Component  │ Description                              │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Mitigation                                      │
  ├──────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────┼──────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Spoofing     │ Auth API   │ Attacker attempts credential stuffing or │ High       │ High     │ Rate Limiting (Redis), strict password hashing  │
  │              │            │ session hijacking.                       │            │          │ (bcrypt r12), HttpOnly secure cookies.          │
  │ Tampering    │ S3 Uploads │ Attacker alters receipt metadata or      │ Medium     │ Medium   │ Strict MIME-type checking, file size limits on  │
  │              │            │ uploads malware via pre-signed URL.      │            │          │ S3 bucket policy, anti-virus scanning on S3.    │
  │ Repudiation  │ Audit Logs │ Malicious admin alters their actions and │ Low        │ Critical │ Move Audit logs into the ACID transaction.      │
  │              │            │ deletes the log.                         │            │          │ Stream logs to immutable WORM (Write Once Read  │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Many) storage.                                  │
  │ Information  │ API (IDOR) │ Employee A requests Employee B's expense │ Medium     │ High     │ Enforce company_id and user_id context          │
  │ Disclosure   │            │ via /expenses/:id.                       │            │          │ validation at the DB query level (Tenant        │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Isolation).                                     │
  │ Denial of    │ API        │ Attacker requests massive payload to     │ High       │ Medium   │ Custom efficient BigInt serialization, strict   │
  │ Service      │ (BigInt)   │ CPU-starve the Fastify serializer.       │            │          │ pagination limits (take: 50), IP Rate Limiting. │
  │ Elevation of │ State      │ Employee bypasses Manager and calls POST │ Low        │ Critical │ Strict RBAC middleware (requireManagerUp,       │
  │ Privilege    │ Machine    │ /expenses/:id/mark-paid directly.        │            │          │ requireAdminUp). Server-side state validation.  │
  └──────────────┴────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ATTACK TREE: Financial Theft via Expense Fraud

  Goal: Steal Corporate Funds via the Reimbursement Engine

   1. Bypass Approval Workflow
       - 1.1 Exploit IDOR to approve own expense. (Mitigation: Assert actor.id != expense.submitted_by in Approval logic).
       - 1.2 Elevate privilege to Manager. (Mitigation: Strict RBAC canCreateRole checks).
       - 1.3 Exploit State Machine flaw (call /mark-paid on submitted status). (Mitigation: API enforces ExpenseStatus.approved before payout).
   2. Double-Spend / Replay Attacks
       - 2.1 Replay the mark-paid API request concurrently. (Mitigation: Pessimistic locking SELECT FOR UPDATE in Ledger, Idempotency Keys).
       - 2.2 Re-submit the same receipt multiple times. (Mitigation: OCR hash matching to detect duplicate receipts across the company).
   3. Malicious Corporate Onboarding
       - 3.1 Register fake company, bootstrap ledger, simulate fake expenses. (Mitigation: KYC/KYB checks required before Nodal Payout Account is activated
         for real money).

  ---

  5. RISK REGISTER (Prioritized)

  ┌────┬─────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────┬────────────┬──────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬────────┐
  │ ID │ Vulnerability / Risk                    │ Severity │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Remediation Strategy                                     │ Status │
  ├────┼─────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────────┼──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ R1 │ Self-Approval IDOR <br> A Manager/Admin │ Critical │ High       │ Critical │ Modify ExpensesService.approveExpense to throw           │ Open   │
  │    │ submits an expense and approves it      │          │            │          │ ForbiddenError if actor.userId == expense.submitted_by.  │        │
  │    │ themselves, bypassing dual-control.     │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R2 │ Race Condition on Payout (mark-paid)    │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Ensure ExpensesService.markPaid updates state and calls  │ Open   │
  │    │ <br> Concurrent requests to mark an     │          │            │          │ createJournalGroup in the same serializable ACID         │        │
  │    │ expense as paid could result in double  │          │            │          │ transaction. Add Idempotency Keys to the controller      │        │
  │    │ journal entries.                        │          │            │          │ layer.                                                   │        │
  │ R3 │ Unbound S3 Pre-signed URLs <br>         │ High     │ High       │ Med      │ Add Content-Length-Range conditions to the S3 pre-signed │ Open   │
  │    │ Generated URLs do not restrict content  │          │            │          │ POST policy.                                             │        │
  │    │ length or strictly enforce file type at │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ the AWS level.                          │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R4 │ Audit Log Evasion <br> Audit logging is │ High     │ Low        │ High     │ Integrate AuditService.log into the main                 │ Open   │
  │    │ fire-and-forget. DB transaction         │          │            │          │ prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => { ... }) context.      │        │
  │    │ rollback does not rollback the audit    │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ attempt, or vice-versa.                 │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R5 │ Ledger Float Manipulation <br>          │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Enforce amount_paise > 0 validation constraint globally  │ Open   │
  │    │ Submitting negative expense amounts to  │          │            │          │ on Zod schemas and DB CHECK constraints.                 │        │
  │    │ artificially inflate the Corporate      │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ Treasury balance.                       │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  └────┴─────────────────────────────────────────┴──────────┴────────────┴──────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴────────┘
  ---

  SUMMARY OF SECURITY POSTURE

  SpendOS has a very strong theoretical architecture (RBAC, Double-Entry Ledger, Idempotency).

  However, the Business Logic Layer currently possesses trust boundary vulnerabilities. Specifically, Separation of Duties (Dual-Control) is theoretically
  possible but not strictly enforced in code (a Manager can approve their own expenses). Furthermore, the gap between API input validation and DB
  constraints means edge cases (negative amounts, zero amounts) could corrupt the ledger.

  Immediate Action Required: Address R1 (Self-Approval), R2 (Double-Spend), and R5 (Negative Expenses) before moving to beta.

✦ SYSTEM DISCOVERY REPORT: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Status: FINAL (System Discovery Complete)

  ---

  BUSINESS PURPOSE

  Product Overview
  SpendOS is an enterprise-grade financial operations platform designed for high-integrity expense management. It prioritizes financial correctness through
  a ledger-first architecture, ensuring that every business event is backed by a double-entry accounting record.

  Problem Solved
   - Trust Gap: Traditional expense tools often lack a verifiable audit trail that matches actual money movement.
   - Approval Chaos: High-growth companies struggle with role-based visibility and strict state machine transitions for expenses.
   - Financial Integrity: Prevents "ghost" transactions or unbalanced books by enforcing Debits == Credits at the database level.

  User Personas
   1. Black Card (Owner/Founder): Full authority, manages company-wide settings and role creation.
   2. Admin (Operations Lead): Manages teams, freezes accounts, and overrides settings.
   3. Manager (Finance/Senior Ops): Approves expenses and manages the review queue.
   4. Employee (User): Submits expenses and raises tickets for payment delays.

  ---

  TECH STACK

  ┌──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Layer                │ Technology                                       │
  ├──────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Frontend             │ Next.js 15 (App Router), TypeScript, Vanilla CSS │
  │ Backend              │ Fastify (Node.js), TypeScript                    │
  │ Database             │ PostgreSQL (Neon), Prisma ORM                    │
  │ Ledger Engine        │ Custom Double-Entry Core (@spendos/ledger)       │
  │ Authentication       │ JWT (Access/Refresh Tokens), @spendos/auth       │
  │ Caching              │ Redis (Rate limiting, Pulse cache)               │
  │ Cloud/Infrastructure │ AWS S3 (Documents), Resend (Email), Docker       │
  │ Background Jobs      │ Node-cron (SLA), Outbox Processor (Reliability)  │
  └──────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  SYSTEM COMPONENTS

  1. Component Inventory

  ┌──────────────┬───────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Component    │ Path                  │ Description                                                              │
  ├──────────────┼───────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Dashboard    │ apps/dashboard        │ Next.js SPA for all user roles.                                          │
  │ API          │ apps/api              │ Fastify backend providing RESTful endpoints.                             │
  │ Ledger Core  │ packages/ledger       │ The "Heart" of the system; handles atomic double-entry journal postings. │
  │ Auth Lib     │ packages/auth         │ Centralized JWT signing, verification, and rotation logic.               │
  │ Database     │ packages/database     │ Prisma schema and generated client for PostgreSQL.                       │
  │ Shared Types │ packages/shared-types │ Unified TypeScript interfaces across apps.                               │
  └──────────────┴───────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  2. Dependency Map

    1 graph TD
    2     Dashboard[apps/dashboard] --> API[apps/api]
    3     API --> Auth[packages/auth]
    4     API --> Ledger[packages/ledger]
    5     API --> Database[packages/database]
    6     API --> Shared[packages/shared-types]
    7     Ledger --> Database
    8     Database --> Prisma[(PostgreSQL)]
    9     API --> Redis[(Redis)]
   10     API --> S3[AWS S3]
   11     API --> Resend[Email Service]

  3. Request Flow Diagram

    1 [User Action: Submit Expense]
    2        │
    3        ▼
    4 [Dashboard (Next.js)] ─── POST /api/v1/expenses ───► [API (Fastify)]
    5                                                         │
    6        ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
    7        ▼                                                ▼
    8 [Auth Middleware] ◄──── Verify JWT ─────────── [RBAC Guard] ◄──── Check Role
    9        │
   10        ▼
   11 [ExpensesService.createExpense]
   12        │
   13        ├─► [PolicyEngine] ──── Check Auto-Approve?
   14        ├─► [Prisma] ────────── INSERT Expense (Status: submitted)
   15        ├─► [AuditService] ──── Log Event
   16        └─► [OutboxEvent] ───── Create 'expense_submitted' event
   17                                                         │
   18        ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   19        ▼
   20 [Response 201 Created] ───► [Dashboard]

  4. Authentication Flow Diagram

   1 1. [User] ────── Login Credentials ────────► [API]
   2 2. [API] ─────── bcrypt.verify ──────────► [Database]
   3 3. [API] ─────── Sign JWT ───────────────► [Auth Lib]
   4 4. [API] ◄────── Set HttpOnly Cookies ─── [User Browser]
   5    (accessToken, refreshToken)
   6 5. Subsequent Requests: [Browser] ──── (Cookies) ────► [API]
   7 6. Token Expired? [Dashboard] ──── POST /refresh ────► [API] ───► Rotate Tokens

  5. Data Flow Diagram (The Ledger)

    1 [Expense Payment Action]
    2        │
    3        ▼
    4 [API: markPaid]
    5        │
    6        ▼
    7 [Transaction Start (Postgres ACID)]
    8        │
    9        ├─► UPDATE Expense SET status = 'paid'
   10        ├─► [LedgerCore.createJournalGroupWithTx]
   11        │     │
   12        │     ├─► SELECT FOR UPDATE Accounts (Locking)
   13        │     ├─► INSERT JournalGroup (TX metadata)
   14        │     ├─► INSERT JournalEntry (DEBIT: Corporate Expense)
   15        │     └─► INSERT JournalEntry (CREDIT: Corporate Treasury)
   16        │
   17        ├─► INSERT OutboxEvent ('expense_paid')
   18        └─► COMMIT
   19                │
   20                ▼
   21 [OutboxProcessor] ───► [NotificationsService] ───► [User Dashboard]

  ---

  MODULE EXPLANATIONS

  Core Engine: @spendos/ledger
   - Purpose: Ensures transactional integrity for all financial movements.
   - Inputs: Account IDs, Transaction Type, Amount (Paise), Actor ID.
   - Outputs: Balanced JournalGroup and JournalEntries.
   - Dependencies: @spendos/database (Prisma).

  Lifecycle Service: ExpensesService
   - Purpose: Orchestrates the complex expense state machine.
   - Inputs: Submitter Actor, Amount, Category, Proof Documents.
   - Outputs: Expense record, Audit logs, Outbox events.
   - Dependencies: Ledger, PolicyEngine, S3, Notifications.

  Reliability Service: OutboxProcessor
   - Purpose: Guarantees that side effects (Emails, Notifications) occur exactly once, even if the API crashes.
   - Inputs: Pending OutboxEvent records.
   - Outputs: Outgoing emails, in-app notifications.
   - Dependencies: Prisma (FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED), EmailService.

  ---

  CODE HYGIENE & TECHNICAL DEBT

  Dead Code / Unused Services
   - OcrService (ocr.service.ts): Implemented using Tesseract.js but currently orphaned. It has a standalone route (POST /expenses/ocr) but is not
     integrated into the standard expense submission workflow.

  Incomplete Features
   - cleanupStaleLocks (cron.ts): Currently a placeholder. The system supports "review locks" (pessimistic locking in UI) but lacks the automatic cleanup
     for abandoned sessions.
   - Soft-Lock Schema: While server.ts checks for review_locked_by, the schema in schema.prisma has some fields but the logic for expiring them is not yet
     fully production-hardened.

  Experimental Code
   - antigravity-plugin/: Contains "Agents" and "Skills" markdown files. This appears to be a meta-layer for AI-assisted development or automated
     governance, rather than runtime application code.

  ---

  NEXT STEPS: System discovery is complete. The system is well-structured, follow-on tasks should focus on integrating the OCR service or completing the
  stale lock cleanup logic.

  Performing a Senior Architect Review of the SpendOS codebase to identify and classify architectural issues, tech debt, and scaling bottlenecks.

  ✓  ReadFile  spend...\...\expenses.controller.ts
  ✓  ReadFile  spe...\...\notifications.service.ts

✦ SENIOR ARCHITECT REVIEW: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
  SpendOS has a strong foundation with its Ledger-First approach and Outbox Pattern. However, the implementation suffers from significant coupling between
  business logic and infrastructure, and several P0 scalability and reliability bottlenecks that will manifest under moderate load.

  ---

  2. ARCHITECTURAL FINDINGS

  [P0] Critical Vulnerabilities & Bottlenecks

  F1: Outbox Pattern "Processor-per-Instance" Conflict
   - Issue: The startOutboxWorker in server.ts runs a setInterval loop in every API pod. While it uses FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED, there is no coordination for
     event processing that has side effects (like sending emails via Resend).
   - Risk: Race conditions and duplicate external side effects (double emails) if the database doesn't lock fast enough across distributed nodes.
   - Fix: Extract the Outbox Processor into a standalone worker service or use a dedicated queue (Redis/BullMQ) to ensure single-responsibility processing.

  F2: Synchronous External Dependencies in Auth Flow
   - Issue: AuthService.register performs a ledger bootstrap and a database write, but other services (like UsersService.inviteUser) call sendEmail
     synchronously.
   - Risk: If the email provider (Resend) is slow or down, the user's request hangs, potentially timing out the database transaction.
   - Fix: Move all external side effects (Email, Slack, SMS) to the Outbox Pattern. Services should only write to OutboxEvent.

  F3: BigInt Serialization Overhead
   - Issue: The global setReplySerializer in server.ts uses a recursive JSON.stringify with a replacer for BigInt.
   - Risk: Extreme CPU overhead and latency for large responses (e.g., listing 100 journal entries), as it essentially double-serializes every response.
   - Fix: Use a custom JSON stringifier that handles BigInt natively or transform BigInt to string at the Service/DTO layer before serialization.

  ---

  [P1] Structural Design & Coupling

  F4: Service-to-Service Circular Coupling
   - Issue: ExpensesService depends on NotificationsService, and NotificationsService often references Expenses. There is no clear event-driven boundary.
   - Risk: Difficult to unit test in isolation and prone to circular dependency errors as the system grows.
   - Fix: Implement an Internal Event Bus. ExpensesService should emit an event; NotificationsService should listen.

  F5: Missing Aggregate Roots (Data Ownership)
   - Issue: The Ledger package is used directly by AuthService (for bootstrap) and ExpensesService (for payout). Business logic for "Account Creation" is
     scattered.
   - Risk: Violation of Data Ownership. If the ledger schema changes, multiple unrelated services break.
   - Fix: Create a FinancialOrchestrator that owns the relationship between "Business Entities" (Companies/Users) and "Financial Entities" (Accounts).

  ---

  [P2] Scalability & Efficiency

  F6: Audit Logging "Fire and Forget" Anti-pattern
   - Issue: AuditService.log uses an async call without await in many places (fire-and-forget).
   - Risk: Under high load, the Node.js event loop will be flooded with un-awaited promises. If the process crashes, audit logs are lost (Security Breach).
   - Fix: Audit logs are critical for compliance. They must be part of the ACID transaction or written to a reliable log-buffer (like Kafka or a local Redis
     stream).

  F7: Redis "Pulse" Cache Invalidation
   - Issue: activity.service.ts caches the "Dashboard Pulse" for 300s but invalidates it manually in ExpensesService.approveExpense.
   - Risk: Manual invalidation is fragile. Adding a new status or action will lead to stale dashboards.
   - Fix: Use Key Versioning or event-driven invalidation via the Outbox worker.

  ---

  3. CLASSIFIED REMEDIATION PLAN

  ┌────┬───────┬───────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ ID │ Class │ Title             │ Recommended Action                                          │
  ├────┼───────┼───────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ F1 │ P0    │ Outbox Scaling    │ Separate apps/worker from apps/api. Use BullMQ.             │
  │ F2 │ P0    │ Sync Side-Effects │ Audit all services; move sendEmail to Outbox.               │
  │ F3 │ P0    │ BigInt Perf       │ Implement bigint-json-serialization package.                │
  │ F4 │ P1    │ Circular Deps     │ Introduce EventEmitter2 or similar for cross-service comms. │
  │ F5 │ P1    │ Ledger Boundary   │ Move account seeding to LedgerService factory.              │
  │ F6 │ P2    │ Audit Integrity   │ Wrap AuditLog in the primary Prisma transaction.            │
  └────┴───────┴───────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ARCHITECTURAL SCORECARD

   - Separation of Concerns: B- (Business logic is leaking into controllers).
   - Coupling: C (High coupling between Domain and Infrastructure).
   - Cohesion: A- (Ledger logic is very cohesive).
   - API Design: B+ (Good use of Zod and Fastify Type Providers).
   - Scalability: C- (Outbox and BigInt issues will cause early failure).

  ---

  FINAL VERDICT: The "Ledger-First" strategy is a winner. The "Outbox" implementation is the weakest link. Fix F1 and F2 immediately to ensure production
  readiness.

  Security Architecture: Threat Modeling: Acting as a Security Architect to create a comprehensive threat model for the SpendOS application.


✦ SECURITY ARCHITECTURE REVIEW & THREAT MODEL

  Author: Security Architect
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target: SpendOS (Expense Reimbursement Engine & Ledger)

  ---

  1. ASSETS & TRUST BOUNDARIES

  1.1 Critical Assets
   1. The Ledger (System of Truth): JournalGroups and JournalEntries. Modification outside business rules equates to financial loss.
   2. Corporate Funds: Bank accounts linked to the Nodal Payout Account.
   3. PII & Identity Data: User emails, GSTINs, full names, password hashes.
   4. Expense Proof (Receipts): S3 Buckets containing potentially sensitive corporate spending data.
   5. Audit Logs: Irrefutable record of who did what.

  1.2 Trust Boundaries
   - TB-1: Internet ↔ Web Dashboard / Mobile: Untrusted client communicating with trusted frontend layer.
   - TB-2: Client ↔ API Gateway (Fastify): Untrusted payload entering the validation/auth boundary.
   - TB-3: API ↔ Database (Postgres): Trusted application executing logic against the persistence layer.
   - TB-4: API ↔ AWS S3: Direct client upload via pre-signed URLs (Semi-trusted interaction).
   - TB-5: Tenant ↔ Tenant: Strict logical boundary between company_A and company_B.

  ---

  2. ENTRY POINTS & ATTACK SURFACES

  2.1 Attack Surfaces
   1. Authentication & Session Management: /api/v1/auth/*
   2. Expense State Machine: /api/v1/expenses/:id/* (Approve, Reject, Mark Paid)
   3. File Uploads: S3 Pre-signed URL generation and confirmation.
   4. Role-Based Access Control (RBAC): API endpoint guards.
   5. Cross-Tenant Data Access (IDOR): Direct object references in APIs.

  2.2 Entry Points
   - Public API Routes (/login, /register, /invite).
   - Authenticated API Routes (Mutations like POST /expenses).
   - Direct S3 Upload endpoints.

  ---

  3. DATA FLOW THREAT MODEL (STRIDE)

  ┌──────────────┬────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Threat       │ Component  │ Description                              │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Mitigation                                      │
  ├──────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────┼──────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Spoofing     │ Auth API   │ Attacker attempts credential stuffing or │ High       │ High     │ Rate Limiting (Redis), strict password hashing  │
  │              │            │ session hijacking.                       │            │          │ (bcrypt r12), HttpOnly secure cookies.          │
  │ Tampering    │ S3 Uploads │ Attacker alters receipt metadata or      │ Medium     │ Medium   │ Strict MIME-type checking, file size limits on  │
  │              │            │ uploads malware via pre-signed URL.      │            │          │ S3 bucket policy, anti-virus scanning on S3.    │
  │ Repudiation  │ Audit Logs │ Malicious admin alters their actions and │ Low        │ Critical │ Move Audit logs into the ACID transaction.      │
  │              │            │ deletes the log.                         │            │          │ Stream logs to immutable WORM (Write Once Read  │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Many) storage.                                  │
  │ Information  │ API (IDOR) │ Employee A requests Employee B's expense │ Medium     │ High     │ Enforce company_id and user_id context          │
  │ Disclosure   │            │ via /expenses/:id.                       │            │          │ validation at the DB query level (Tenant        │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Isolation).                                     │
  │ Denial of    │ API        │ Attacker requests massive payload to     │ High       │ Medium   │ Custom efficient BigInt serialization, strict   │
  │ Service      │ (BigInt)   │ CPU-starve the Fastify serializer.       │            │          │ pagination limits (take: 50), IP Rate Limiting. │
  │ Elevation of │ State      │ Employee bypasses Manager and calls POST │ Low        │ Critical │ Strict RBAC middleware (requireManagerUp,       │
  │ Privilege    │ Machine    │ /expenses/:id/mark-paid directly.        │            │          │ requireAdminUp). Server-side state validation.  │
  └──────────────┴────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ATTACK TREE: Financial Theft via Expense Fraud

  Goal: Steal Corporate Funds via the Reimbursement Engine

   1. Bypass Approval Workflow
       - 1.1 Exploit IDOR to approve own expense. (Mitigation: Assert actor.id != expense.submitted_by in Approval logic).
       - 1.2 Elevate privilege to Manager. (Mitigation: Strict RBAC canCreateRole checks).
       - 1.3 Exploit State Machine flaw (call /mark-paid on submitted status). (Mitigation: API enforces ExpenseStatus.approved before payout).
   2. Double-Spend / Replay Attacks
       - 2.1 Replay the mark-paid API request concurrently. (Mitigation: Pessimistic locking SELECT FOR UPDATE in Ledger, Idempotency Keys).
       - 2.2 Re-submit the same receipt multiple times. (Mitigation: OCR hash matching to detect duplicate receipts across the company).
   3. Malicious Corporate Onboarding
       - 3.1 Register fake company, bootstrap ledger, simulate fake expenses. (Mitigation: KYC/KYB checks required before Nodal Payout Account is activated
         for real money).

  ---

  5. RISK REGISTER (Prioritized)

  ┌────┬─────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────┬────────────┬──────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬────────┐
  │ ID │ Vulnerability / Risk                    │ Severity │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Remediation Strategy                                     │ Status │
  ├────┼─────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────────┼──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ R1 │ Self-Approval IDOR <br> A Manager/Admin │ Critical │ High       │ Critical │ Modify ExpensesService.approveExpense to throw           │ Open   │
  │    │ submits an expense and approves it      │          │            │          │ ForbiddenError if actor.userId == expense.submitted_by.  │        │
  │    │ themselves, bypassing dual-control.     │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R2 │ Race Condition on Payout (mark-paid)    │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Ensure ExpensesService.markPaid updates state and calls  │ Open   │
  │    │ <br> Concurrent requests to mark an     │          │            │          │ createJournalGroup in the same serializable ACID         │        │
  │    │ expense as paid could result in double  │          │            │          │ transaction. Add Idempotency Keys to the controller      │        │
  │    │ journal entries.                        │          │            │          │ layer.                                                   │        │
  │ R3 │ Unbound S3 Pre-signed URLs <br>         │ High     │ High       │ Med      │ Add Content-Length-Range conditions to the S3 pre-signed │ Open   │
  │    │ Generated URLs do not restrict content  │          │            │          │ POST policy.                                             │        │
  │    │ length or strictly enforce file type at │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ the AWS level.                          │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R4 │ Audit Log Evasion <br> Audit logging is │ High     │ Low        │ High     │ Integrate AuditService.log into the main                 │ Open   │
  │    │ fire-and-forget. DB transaction         │          │            │          │ prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => { ... }) context.      │        │
  │    │ rollback does not rollback the audit    │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ attempt, or vice-versa.                 │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R5 │ Ledger Float Manipulation <br>          │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Enforce amount_paise > 0 validation constraint globally  │ Open   │
  │    │ Submitting negative expense amounts to  │          │            │          │ on Zod schemas and DB CHECK constraints.                 │        │
  │    │ artificially inflate the Corporate      │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ Treasury balance.                       │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  └────┴─────────────────────────────────────────┴──────────┴────────────┴──────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴────────┘
  ---

  SUMMARY OF SECURITY POSTURE

  SpendOS has a very strong theoretical architecture (RBAC, Double-Entry Ledger, Idempotency).

  However, the Business Logic Layer currently possesses trust boundary vulnerabilities. Specifically, Separation of Duties (Dual-Control) is theoretically
  possible but not strictly enforced in code (a Manager can approve their own expenses). Furthermore, the gap between API input validation and DB
  constraints means edge cases (negative amounts, zero amounts) could corrupt the ledger.

  Immediate Action Required: Address R1 (Self-Approval), R2 (Double-Spend), and R5 (Negative Expenses) before moving to beta.

✦ SYSTEM DISCOVERY REPORT: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Status: FINAL (System Discovery Complete)

  ---

  BUSINESS PURPOSE

  Product Overview
  SpendOS is an enterprise-grade financial operations platform designed for high-integrity expense management. It prioritizes financial correctness through
  a ledger-first architecture, ensuring that every business event is backed by a double-entry accounting record.

  Problem Solved
   - Trust Gap: Traditional expense tools often lack a verifiable audit trail that matches actual money movement.
   - Approval Chaos: High-growth companies struggle with role-based visibility and strict state machine transitions for expenses.
   - Financial Integrity: Prevents "ghost" transactions or unbalanced books by enforcing Debits == Credits at the database level.

  User Personas
   1. Black Card (Owner/Founder): Full authority, manages company-wide settings and role creation.
   2. Admin (Operations Lead): Manages teams, freezes accounts, and overrides settings.
   3. Manager (Finance/Senior Ops): Approves expenses and manages the review queue.
   4. Employee (User): Submits expenses and raises tickets for payment delays.

  ---

  TECH STACK

  ┌──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Layer                │ Technology                                       │
  ├──────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Frontend             │ Next.js 15 (App Router), TypeScript, Vanilla CSS │
  │ Backend              │ Fastify (Node.js), TypeScript                    │
  │ Database             │ PostgreSQL (Neon), Prisma ORM                    │
  │ Ledger Engine        │ Custom Double-Entry Core (@spendos/ledger)       │
  │ Authentication       │ JWT (Access/Refresh Tokens), @spendos/auth       │
  │ Caching              │ Redis (Rate limiting, Pulse cache)               │
  │ Cloud/Infrastructure │ AWS S3 (Documents), Resend (Email), Docker       │
  │ Background Jobs      │ Node-cron (SLA), Outbox Processor (Reliability)  │
  └──────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  SYSTEM COMPONENTS

  1. Component Inventory

  ┌──────────────┬───────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Component    │ Path                  │ Description                                                              │
  ├──────────────┼───────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Dashboard    │ apps/dashboard        │ Next.js SPA for all user roles.                                          │
  │ API          │ apps/api              │ Fastify backend providing RESTful endpoints.                             │
  │ Ledger Core  │ packages/ledger       │ The "Heart" of the system; handles atomic double-entry journal postings. │
  │ Auth Lib     │ packages/auth         │ Centralized JWT signing, verification, and rotation logic.               │
  │ Database     │ packages/database     │ Prisma schema and generated client for PostgreSQL.                       │
  │ Shared Types │ packages/shared-types │ Unified TypeScript interfaces across apps.                               │
  └──────────────┴───────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  2. Dependency Map

    1 graph TD
    2     Dashboard[apps/dashboard] --> API[apps/api]
    3     API --> Auth[packages/auth]
    4     API --> Ledger[packages/ledger]
    5     API --> Database[packages/database]
    6     API --> Shared[packages/shared-types]
    7     Ledger --> Database
    8     Database --> Prisma[(PostgreSQL)]
    9     API --> Redis[(Redis)]
   10     API --> S3[AWS S3]

    1 [User Action: Submit Expense]

   12        │

   17                                                         │

   20 [Response 201 Created] ───► [Dashboard]

  4. Authentication Flow Diagram

   1 1. [User] ────── Login Credentials ────────► [API]
   2 2. [API] ─────── bcrypt.verify ──────────► [Database]
   3 3. [API] ─────── Sign JWT ───────────────► [Auth Lib]
   4 4. [API] ◄────── Set HttpOnly Cookies ─── [User Browser]

  5. Data Flow Diagram (The Ledger)

    1 [Expense Payment Action]
    2        │
    3        ▼
    4 [API: markPaid]

    9        ├─► UPDATE Expense SET status = 'paid'
   10        ├─► [LedgerCore.createJournalGroupWithTx]
   11        │     │
   12        │     ├─► SELECT FOR UPDATE Accounts (Locking)
   13        │     ├─► INSERT JournalGroup (TX metadata)
   14        │     ├─► INSERT JournalEntry (DEBIT: Corporate Expense)
   15        │     └─► INSERT JournalEntry (CREDIT: Corporate Treasury)
   16        │
   17        ├─► INSERT OutboxEvent ('expense_paid')
   18        └─► COMMIT
   19                │
   20                ▼
   21 [OutboxProcessor] ───► [NotificationsService] ───► [User Dashboard]

  ---

  MODULE EXPLANATIONS

  Core Engine: @spendos/ledger
   - Purpose: Ensures transactional integrity for all financial movements.
   - Inputs: Account IDs, Transaction Type, Amount (Paise), Actor ID.
   - Outputs: Balanced JournalGroup and JournalEntries.
   - Dependencies: @spendos/database (Prisma).

  Lifecycle Service: ExpensesService
   - Purpose: Orchestrates the complex expense state machine.
   - Inputs: Submitter Actor, Amount, Category, Proof Documents.
   - Outputs: Expense record, Audit logs, Outbox events.
   - Dependencies: Ledger, PolicyEngine, S3, Notifications.

  Reliability Service: OutboxProcessor
   - Purpose: Guarantees that side effects (Emails, Notifications) occur exactly once, even if the API crashes.
   - Inputs: Pending OutboxEvent records.
   - Outputs: Outgoing emails, in-app notifications.
   - Dependencies: Prisma (FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED), EmailService.

  ---

  CODE HYGIENE & TECHNICAL DEBT

  Dead Code / Unused Services
   - OcrService (ocr.service.ts): Implemented using Tesseract.js but currently orphaned. It has a standalone route (POST /expenses/ocr) but is not
     integrated into the standard expense submission workflow.

  Incomplete Features
   - cleanupStaleLocks (cron.ts): Currently a placeholder. The system supports "review locks" (pessimistic locking in UI) but lacks the automatic cleanup
     for abandoned sessions.
   - Soft-Lock Schema: While server.ts checks for review_locked_by, the schema in schema.prisma has some fields but the logic for expiring them is not yet
     fully production-hardened.

  Experimental Code
   - antigravity-plugin/: Contains "Agents" and "Skills" markdown files. This appears to be a meta-layer for AI-assisted development or automated
     governance, rather than runtime application code.

  ---

  NEXT STEPS: System discovery is complete. The system is well-structured, follow-on tasks should focus on integrating the OCR service or completing the
  stale lock cleanup logic.

✦ SENIOR ARCHITECT REVIEW: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
  SpendOS has a strong foundation with its Ledger-First approach and Outbox Pattern. However, the implementation suffers from significant coupling between
  business logic and infrastructure, and several P0 scalability and reliability bottlenecks that will manifest under moderate load.

  ---

  2. ARCHITECTURAL FINDINGS

  [P0] Critical Vulnerabilities & Bottlenecks

  F1: Outbox Pattern "Processor-per-Instance" Conflict
   - Issue: The startOutboxWorker in server.ts runs a setInterval loop in every API pod. While it uses FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED, there is no coordination for
     event processing that has side effects (like sending emails via Resend).
   - Risk: Race conditions and duplicate external side effects (double emails) if the database doesn't lock fast enough across distributed nodes.
   - Fix: Extract the Outbox Processor into a standalone worker service or use a dedicated queue (Redis/BullMQ) to ensure single-responsibility processing.

  F2: Synchronous External Dependencies in Auth Flow
   - Issue: AuthService.register performs a ledger bootstrap and a database write, but other services (like UsersService.inviteUser) call sendEmail
     synchronously.
   - Risk: If the email provider (Resend) is slow or down, the user's request hangs, potentially timing out the database transaction.
   - Fix: Move all external side effects (Email, Slack, SMS) to the Outbox Pattern. Services should only write to OutboxEvent.

  F3: BigInt Serialization Overhead
   - Issue: The global setReplySerializer in server.ts uses a recursive JSON.stringify with a replacer for BigInt.
   - Risk: Extreme CPU overhead and latency for large responses (e.g., listing 100 journal entries), as it essentially double-serializes every response.
   - Fix: Use a custom JSON stringifier that handles BigInt natively or transform BigInt to string at the Service/DTO layer before serialization.

  ---

  [P1] Structural Design & Coupling

  F4: Service-to-Service Circular Coupling
   - Issue: ExpensesService depends on NotificationsService, and NotificationsService often references Expenses. There is no clear event-driven boundary.
   - Risk: Difficult to unit test in isolation and prone to circular dependency errors as the system grows.
   - Fix: Implement an Internal Event Bus. ExpensesService should emit an event; NotificationsService should listen.

  F5: Missing Aggregate Roots (Data Ownership)
   - Issue: The Ledger package is used directly by AuthService (for bootstrap) and ExpensesService (for payout). Business logic for "Account Creation" is
     scattered.
   - Risk: Violation of Data Ownership. If the ledger schema changes, multiple unrelated services break.
   - Fix: Create a FinancialOrchestrator that owns the relationship between "Business Entities" (Companies/Users) and "Financial Entities" (Accounts).

  ---

  [P2] Scalability & Efficiency

  F6: Audit Logging "Fire and Forget" Anti-pattern
   - Issue: AuditService.log uses an async call without await in many places (fire-and-forget).
   - Risk: Under high load, the Node.js event loop will be flooded with un-awaited promises. If the process crashes, audit logs are lost (Security Breach).
   - Fix: Audit logs are critical for compliance. They must be part of the ACID transaction or written to a reliable log-buffer (like Kafka or a local Redis
     stream).

  F7: Redis "Pulse" Cache Invalidation
   - Issue: activity.service.ts caches the "Dashboard Pulse" for 300s but invalidates it manually in ExpensesService.approveExpense.
   - Risk: Manual invalidation is fragile. Adding a new status or action will lead to stale dashboards.
   - Fix: Use Key Versioning or event-driven invalidation via the Outbox worker.

  ---

  3. CLASSIFIED REMEDIATION PLAN

  ┌────┬───────┬───────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ ID │ Class │ Title             │ Recommended Action                                          │
  ├────┼───────┼───────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ F1 │ P0    │ Outbox Scaling    │ Separate apps/worker from apps/api. Use BullMQ.             │
  │ F2 │ P0    │ Sync Side-Effects │ Audit all services; move sendEmail to Outbox.               │
  │ F3 │ P0    │ BigInt Perf       │ Implement bigint-json-serialization package.                │
  │ F4 │ P1    │ Circular Deps     │ Introduce EventEmitter2 or similar for cross-service comms. │
  │ F5 │ P1    │ Ledger Boundary   │ Move account seeding to LedgerService factory.              │
  │ F6 │ P2    │ Audit Integrity   │ Wrap AuditLog in the primary Prisma transaction.            │
  └────┴───────┴───────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ARCHITECTURAL SCORECARD

   - Separation of Concerns: B- (Business logic is leaking into controllers).
   - Coupling: C (High coupling between Domain and Infrastructure).
   - Cohesion: A- (Ledger logic is very cohesive).
   - API Design: B+ (Good use of Zod and Fastify Type Providers).
   - Scalability: C- (Outbox and BigInt issues will cause early failure).

  ---

  FINAL VERDICT: The "Ledger-First" strategy is a winner. The "Outbox" implementation is the weakest link. Fix F1 and F2 immediately to ensure production
  readiness.
▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄

  Security Architecture: Threat Modeling: Acting as a Security Architect to create a comprehensive threat model for the SpendOS application.


✦ SECURITY ARCHITECTURE REVIEW & THREAT MODEL

  Author: Security Architect
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target: SpendOS (Expense Reimbursement Engine & Ledger)

  ---

  1. ASSETS & TRUST BOUNDARIES

  1.1 Critical Assets
   1. The Ledger (System of Truth): JournalGroups and JournalEntries. Modification outside business rules equates to financial loss.
   2. Corporate Funds: Bank accounts linked to the Nodal Payout Account.
   3. PII & Identity Data: User emails, GSTINs, full names, password hashes.
   4. Expense Proof (Receipts): S3 Buckets containing potentially sensitive corporate spending data.
   5. Audit Logs: Irrefutable record of who did what.

  1.2 Trust Boundaries
   - TB-1: Internet ↔ Web Dashboard / Mobile: Untrusted client communicating with trusted frontend layer.
   - TB-2: Client ↔ API Gateway (Fastify): Untrusted payload entering the validation/auth boundary.
   - TB-3: API ↔ Database (Postgres): Trusted application executing logic against the persistence layer.
   - TB-4: API ↔ AWS S3: Direct client upload via pre-signed URLs (Semi-trusted interaction).
   - TB-5: Tenant ↔ Tenant: Strict logical boundary between company_A and company_B.

  ---

  2. ENTRY POINTS & ATTACK SURFACES

  2.1 Attack Surfaces
   1. Authentication & Session Management: /api/v1/auth/*
   2. Expense State Machine: /api/v1/expenses/:id/* (Approve, Reject, Mark Paid)
   3. File Uploads: S3 Pre-signed URL generation and confirmation.
   4. Role-Based Access Control (RBAC): API endpoint guards.
   5. Cross-Tenant Data Access (IDOR): Direct object references in APIs.

  2.2 Entry Points
   - Public API Routes (/login, /register, /invite).
   - Authenticated API Routes (Mutations like POST /expenses).
   - Direct S3 Upload endpoints.

  ---

  3. DATA FLOW THREAT MODEL (STRIDE)

  ┌──────────────┬────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┬────────────┬──────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Threat       │ Component  │ Description                              │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Mitigation                                      │
  ├──────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┼────────────┼──────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Spoofing     │ Auth API   │ Attacker attempts credential stuffing or │ High       │ High     │ Rate Limiting (Redis), strict password hashing  │
  │              │            │ session hijacking.                       │            │          │ (bcrypt r12), HttpOnly secure cookies.          │
  │ Tampering    │ S3 Uploads │ Attacker alters receipt metadata or      │ Medium     │ Medium   │ Strict MIME-type checking, file size limits on  │
  │              │            │ uploads malware via pre-signed URL.      │            │          │ S3 bucket policy, anti-virus scanning on S3.    │
  │ Repudiation  │ Audit Logs │ Malicious admin alters their actions and │ Low        │ Critical │ Move Audit logs into the ACID transaction.      │
  │              │            │ deletes the log.                         │            │          │ Stream logs to immutable WORM (Write Once Read  │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Many) storage.                                  │
  │ Information  │ API (IDOR) │ Employee A requests Employee B's expense │ Medium     │ High     │ Enforce company_id and user_id context          │
  │ Disclosure   │            │ via /expenses/:id.                       │            │          │ validation at the DB query level (Tenant        │
  │              │            │                                          │            │          │ Isolation).                                     │
  │ Denial of    │ API        │ Attacker requests massive payload to     │ High       │ Medium   │ Custom efficient BigInt serialization, strict   │
  │ Service      │ (BigInt)   │ CPU-starve the Fastify serializer.       │            │          │ pagination limits (take: 50), IP Rate Limiting. │
  │ Elevation of │ State      │ Employee bypasses Manager and calls POST │ Low        │ Critical │ Strict RBAC middleware (requireManagerUp,       │
  │ Privilege    │ Machine    │ /expenses/:id/mark-paid directly.        │            │          │ requireAdminUp). Server-side state validation.  │
  └──────────────┴────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┴────────────┴──────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ATTACK TREE: Financial Theft via Expense Fraud

  Goal: Steal Corporate Funds via the Reimbursement Engine

   1. Bypass Approval Workflow
       - 1.1 Exploit IDOR to approve own expense. (Mitigation: Assert actor.id != expense.submitted_by in Approval logic).
       - 1.2 Elevate privilege to Manager. (Mitigation: Strict RBAC canCreateRole checks).
       - 1.3 Exploit State Machine flaw (call /mark-paid on submitted status). (Mitigation: API enforces ExpenseStatus.approved before payout).
   2. Double-Spend / Replay Attacks
       - 2.1 Replay the mark-paid API request concurrently. (Mitigation: Pessimistic locking SELECT FOR UPDATE in Ledger, Idempotency Keys).
       - 2.2 Re-submit the same receipt multiple times. (Mitigation: OCR hash matching to detect duplicate receipts across the company).
   3. Malicious Corporate Onboarding
       - 3.1 Register fake company, bootstrap ledger, simulate fake expenses. (Mitigation: KYC/KYB checks required before Nodal Payout Account is activated
         for real money).

  ---

  5. RISK REGISTER (Prioritized)

  ┌────┬─────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────┬────────────┬──────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬────────┐
  │ ID │ Vulnerability / Risk                    │ Severity │ Likelihood │ Impact   │ Remediation Strategy                                     │ Status │
  ├────┼─────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────────┼──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼────────┤
  │ R1 │ Self-Approval IDOR <br> A Manager/Admin │ Critical │ High       │ Critical │ Modify ExpensesService.approveExpense to throw           │ Open   │
  │    │ submits an expense and approves it      │          │            │          │ ForbiddenError if actor.userId == expense.submitted_by.  │        │
  │    │ themselves, bypassing dual-control.     │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R2 │ Race Condition on Payout (mark-paid)    │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Ensure ExpensesService.markPaid updates state and calls  │ Open   │
  │    │ <br> Concurrent requests to mark an     │          │            │          │ createJournalGroup in the same serializable ACID         │        │
  │    │ expense as paid could result in double  │          │            │          │ transaction. Add Idempotency Keys to the controller      │        │
  │    │ journal entries.                        │          │            │          │ layer.                                                   │        │
  │ R3 │ Unbound S3 Pre-signed URLs <br>         │ High     │ High       │ Med      │ Add Content-Length-Range conditions to the S3 pre-signed │ Open   │
  │    │ Generated URLs do not restrict content  │          │            │          │ POST policy.                                             │        │
  │    │ length or strictly enforce file type at │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ the AWS level.                          │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R4 │ Audit Log Evasion <br> Audit logging is │ High     │ Low        │ High     │ Integrate AuditService.log into the main                 │ Open   │
  │    │ fire-and-forget. DB transaction         │          │            │          │ prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => { ... }) context.      │        │
  │    │ rollback does not rollback the audit    │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ attempt, or vice-versa.                 │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │ R5 │ Ledger Float Manipulation <br>          │ Critical │ Med        │ Critical │ Enforce amount_paise > 0 validation constraint globally  │ Open   │
  │    │ Submitting negative expense amounts to  │          │            │          │ on Zod schemas and DB CHECK constraints.                 │        │
  │    │ artificially inflate the Corporate      │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  │    │ Treasury balance.                       │          │            │          │                                                          │        │
  └────┴─────────────────────────────────────────┴──────────┴────────────┴──────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴────────┘
  ---

  SUMMARY OF SECURITY POSTURE

  SpendOS has a very strong theoretical architecture (RBAC, Double-Entry Ledger, Idempotency).

  However, the Business Logic Layer currently possesses trust boundary vulnerabilities. Specifically, Separation of Duties (Dual-Control) is theoretically
  possible but not strictly enforced in code (a Manager can approve their own expenses). Furthermore, the gap between API input validation and DB
  constraints means edge cases (negative amounts, zero amounts) could corrupt the ledger.

  Immediate Action Required: Address R1 (Self-Approval), R2 (Double-Spend), and R5 (Negative Expenses) before moving to beta.

 > You are a Principal Systems Engineer.

   Your first task is NOT to audit.

   Your first task is to understand the entire system.

   Study the codebase and create a SYSTEM DISCOVERY REPORT.

   Determine:

   BUSINESS PURPOSE
   - What product is this?
   - What problem does it solve?
   - Who are the users?

   TECH STACK
   - Frontend

✦ SYSTEM DISCOVERY REPORT: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Status: FINAL (System Discovery Complete)

  ---

  BUSINESS PURPOSE

  Product Overview
  SpendOS is an enterprise-grade financial operations platform designed for high-integrity expense management. It prioritizes financial correctness through
  a ledger-first architecture, ensuring that every business event is backed by a double-entry accounting record.

  Problem Solved
   - Trust Gap: Traditional expense tools often lack a verifiable audit trail that matches actual money movement.
   - Approval Chaos: High-growth companies struggle with role-based visibility and strict state machine transitions for expenses.
   - Financial Integrity: Prevents "ghost" transactions or unbalanced books by enforcing Debits == Credits at the database level.

  User Personas
   1. Black Card (Owner/Founder): Full authority, manages company-wide settings and role creation.
   2. Admin (Operations Lead): Manages teams, freezes accounts, and overrides settings.
   3. Manager (Finance/Senior Ops): Approves expenses and manages the review queue.
   4. Employee (User): Submits expenses and raises tickets for payment delays.

  ---

  TECH STACK

  ┌──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Layer                │ Technology                                       │
  ├──────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Frontend             │ Next.js 15 (App Router), TypeScript, Vanilla CSS │
  │ Backend              │ Fastify (Node.js), TypeScript                    │
  │ Database             │ PostgreSQL (Neon), Prisma ORM                    │
  │ Ledger Engine        │ Custom Double-Entry Core (@spendos/ledger)       │
  │ Authentication       │ JWT (Access/Refresh Tokens), @spendos/auth       │
  │ Caching              │ Redis (Rate limiting, Pulse cache)               │
  │ Cloud/Infrastructure │ AWS S3 (Documents), Resend (Email), Docker       │
  │ Background Jobs      │ Node-cron (SLA), Outbox Processor (Reliability)  │
  └──────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  SYSTEM COMPONENTS

  │ Database     │ packages/database     │ Prisma schema and generated client for PostgreSQL.                       │

   15        │     └─► INSERT JournalEntry (CREDIT: Corporate Treasury)

   19                │

   21 [OutboxProcessor] ───► [NotificationsService] ───► [User Dashboard]

  ---

  MODULE EXPLANATIONS

  Core Engine: @spendos/ledger
   - Purpose: Ensures transactional integrity for all financial movements.
   - Inputs: Account IDs, Transaction Type, Amount (Paise), Actor ID.
   - Outputs: Balanced JournalGroup and JournalEntries.
   - Dependencies: @spendos/database (Prisma).

  Lifecycle Service: ExpensesService
   - Purpose: Orchestrates the complex expense state machine.
   - Inputs: Submitter Actor, Amount, Category, Proof Documents.
   - Outputs: Expense record, Audit logs, Outbox events.
   - Dependencies: Ledger, PolicyEngine, S3, Notifications.

  Reliability Service: OutboxProcessor
   - Purpose: Guarantees that side effects (Emails, Notifications) occur exactly once, even if the API crashes.
   - Inputs: Pending OutboxEvent records.
   - Outputs: Outgoing emails, in-app notifications.
   - Dependencies: Prisma (FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED), EmailService.

  ---

  CODE HYGIENE & TECHNICAL DEBT

  Dead Code / Unused Services
   - OcrService (ocr.service.ts): Implemented using Tesseract.js but currently orphaned. It has a standalone route (POST /expenses/ocr) but is not
     integrated into the standard expense submission workflow.

  Incomplete Features
   - cleanupStaleLocks (cron.ts): Currently a placeholder. The system supports "review locks" (pessimistic locking in UI) but lacks the automatic cleanup
     for abandoned sessions.
   - Soft-Lock Schema: While server.ts checks for review_locked_by, the schema in schema.prisma has some fields but the logic for expiring them is not yet
     fully production-hardened.

  Experimental Code
   - antigravity-plugin/: Contains "Agents" and "Skills" markdown files. This appears to be a meta-layer for AI-assisted development or automated
     governance, rather than runtime application code.

  ---

  NEXT STEPS: System discovery is complete. The system is well-structured, follow-on tasks should focus on integrating the OCR service or completing the
  stale lock cleanup logic.

✦ SENIOR ARCHITECT REVIEW: SpendOS

  Author: Principal Systems Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
  SpendOS has a strong foundation with its Ledger-First approach and Outbox Pattern. However, the implementation suffers from significant coupling between
  business logic and infrastructure, and several P0 scalability and reliability bottlenecks that will manifest under moderate load.

  ---

  2. ARCHITECTURAL FINDINGS

  [P0] Critical Vulnerabilities & Bottlenecks

  F1: Outbox Pattern "Processor-per-Instance" Conflict
   - Issue: The startOutboxWorker in server.ts runs a setInterval loop in every API pod. While it uses FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED, there is no coordination for
     event processing that has side effects (like sending emails via Resend).
   - Risk: Race conditions and duplicate external side effects (double emails) if the database doesn't lock fast enough across distributed nodes.
   - Fix: Extract the Outbox Processor into a standalone worker service or use a dedicated queue (Redis/BullMQ) to ensure single-responsibility processing.

  F2: Synchronous External Dependencies in Auth Flow
   - Issue: AuthService.register performs a ledger bootstrap and a database write, but other services (like UsersService.inviteUser) call sendEmail
     synchronously.
   - Risk: If the email provider (Resend) is slow or down, the user's request hangs, potentially timing out the database transaction.
   - Fix: Move all external side effects (Email, Slack, SMS) to the Outbox Pattern. Services should only write to OutboxEvent.

  F3: BigInt Serialization Overhead
   - Issue: The global setReplySerializer in server.ts uses a recursive JSON.stringify with a replacer for BigInt.
   - Risk: Extreme CPU overhead and latency for large responses (e.g., listing 100 journal entries), as it essentially double-serializes every response.
   - Fix: Use a custom JSON stringifier that handles BigInt natively or transform BigInt to string at the Service/DTO layer before serialization.

  ---

  [P1] Structural Design & Coupling

  F4: Service-to-Service Circular Coupling
   - Issue: ExpensesService depends on NotificationsService, and NotificationsService often references Expenses. There is no clear event-driven boundary.
   - Risk: Difficult to unit test in isolation and prone to circular dependency errors as the system grows.
   - Fix: Implement an Internal Event Bus. ExpensesService should emit an event; NotificationsService should listen.

  F5: Missing Aggregate Roots (Data Ownership)
   - Issue: The Ledger package is used directly by AuthService (for bootstrap) and ExpensesService (for payout). Business logic for "Account Creation" is
     scattered.
   - Risk: Violation of Data Ownership. If the ledger schema changes, multiple unrelated services break.
   - Fix: Create a FinancialOrchestrator that owns the relationship between "Business Entities" (Companies/Users) and "Financial Entities" (Accounts).

  ---

  [P2] Scalability & Efficiency

  F6: Audit Logging "Fire and Forget" Anti-pattern
   - Issue: AuditService.log uses an async call without await in many places (fire-and-forget).
   - Risk: Under high load, the Node.js event loop will be flooded with un-awaited promises. If the process crashes, audit logs are lost (Security Breach).
   - Fix: Audit logs are critical for compliance. They must be part of the ACID transaction or written to a reliable log-buffer (like Kafka or a local Redis
     stream).

  F7: Redis "Pulse" Cache Invalidation
   - Issue: activity.service.ts caches the "Dashboard Pulse" for 300s but invalidates it manually in ExpensesService.approveExpense.
   - Risk: Manual invalidation is fragile. Adding a new status or action will lead to stale dashboards.
   - Fix: Use Key Versioning or event-driven invalidation via the Outbox worker.

  ---

  3. CLASSIFIED REMEDIATION PLAN

  ┌────┬───────┬───────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ ID │ Class │ Title             │ Recommended Action                                          │
  ├────┼───────┼───────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ F1 │ P0    │ Outbox Scaling    │ Separate apps/worker from apps/api. Use BullMQ.             │
  │ F2 │ P0    │ Sync Side-Effects │ Audit all services; move sendEmail to Outbox.               │
  │ F3 │ P0    │ BigInt Perf       │ Implement bigint-json-serialization package.                │
  │ F4 │ P1    │ Circular Deps     │ Introduce EventEmitter2 or similar for cross-service comms. │
  │ F5 │ P1    │ Ledger Boundary   │ Move account seeding to LedgerService factory.              │
  │ F6 │ P2    │ Audit Integrity   │ Wrap AuditLog in the primary Prisma transaction.            │
  └────┴───────┴───────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  ---

  4. ARCHITECTURAL SCORECARD

   - Separation of Concerns: B- (Business logic is leaking into controllers).
   - Coupling: C (High coupling between Domain and Infrastructure).
   - Cohesion: A- (Ledger logic is very cohesive).
   - API Design: B+ (Good use of Zod and Fastify Type Providers).
   - Scalability: C- (Outbox and BigInt issues will cause early failure).

  ---

  FINAL VERDICT: The "Ledger-First" strategy is a winner. The "Outbox" implementation is the weakest link. Fix F1 and F2 immediately to ensure production
  readiness.
