✦ FINANCIAL DATA FLOW & DATABASE INTEGRITY AUDIT

  Author: Principal Database Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target: SpendOS (PostgreSQL, Prisma, Ledger Engine)

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

  Can financial records become inconsistent?
  YES. CRITICALLY SO.

  While the core ledger (@spendos/ledger) employs a robust double-checked locking mechanism (SELECT ... FOR UPDATE), the Application Layer (Services) fails
  to respect ACID boundaries and object locking.

  I have identified Data Corruption, Race Conditions (TOCTOU), Missing Transactions, and a Catastrophic Double-Payout Vulnerability where the system
  bypasses its own idempotency guarantees.

  ---

  2. AUDIT FINDINGS: CODE PATHS & VULNERABILITIES

  [CRITICAL] 1. Double Payout via Idempotency Key Mismatch
  Vulnerability: Double Processing / Financial Loss
  Flows: Expense Reimbursement vs Ticket Resolution

  There are two ways to pay an expense: directly via ExpensesService.markPaid or indirectly via TicketsService.resolveTicket(action="mark_paid").

  The Code Path Mismatch:
  In ExpensesService.ts (Line 233):

   1 idempotencyKey: `reimburse-ledger-${expense.id}`,
  In TicketsService.ts (Line 89):

   1 idempotencyKey: `ticket-reimburse-ledger-${ticket.id}`,

  Exploit Scenario:
   1. Expense is Approved. A Ticket is opened due to SLA breach.
   2. Manager A resolves the ticket using mark_paid.
   3. Manager B manually clicks "Mark Paid" on the expense screen at the exact same time.
   4. Because the idempotencyKey strings are different, the Ledger Engine's double-checked lock considers these as two independent financial events.
   5. Both transactions lock the Accounts sequentially.
   6. Result: The Ledger records TWO debit/credit postings for the exact same expense. The Corporate Treasury is drained twice, but the Expense is only
      marked paid once. Severe Ledger Inconsistency.

  [HIGH] 2. TOCTOU Race Condition on State Transitions
  Vulnerability: Inconsistent State / Orphaned Events
  Flows: Approve, Reject, Mark Paid

  The Code Path:
  In ExpensesService.approveExpense (Line 131):

   1 const expense = await prisma.expense.findUnique({ where: { id } }); // outside transaction!
   2 if (!expense) throw new NotFoundError();
   3 if (!validStatus(expense.status)) throw new BadRequestError();
   4
   5 await prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => {
   6   await tx.expense.update({ ... });
   7   await tx.outboxEvent.create({ ... });
   8 });

  Exploit Scenario:
   1. Thread A and Thread B evaluate findUnique concurrently. Both see status = submitted.
   2. Thread A enters $transaction, updates expense to approved, creates expense_approved Outbox Event.
   3. Thread B enters $transaction (or rejectExpense transaction), updates expense to rejected, creates expense_rejected Outbox Event.
   4. Result: The expense database record says "Rejected", but the user receives two emails: "Approved" and "Rejected". The audit log reflects both.

  [HIGH] 3. Missing Transaction Boundaries on Creation & Updates
  Vulnerability: Missing Transactions / Orphaned Records
  Flows: ExpensesService.createExpense, DocumentsService.confirmUpload

  The Code Path:
  In ExpensesService.createExpense (Line 14):

   1 const expense = await prisma.expense.create({ ... }); // 1. DB Write
   2 const { isAutoApproved } = await PoliciesService.evaluateExpense(...);
   3 if (isAutoApproved) {
   4   await prisma.expense.update({ ... });               // 2. DB Write
   5   await AuditService.log({ ... });                    // 3. Fire & Forget DB Write
   6 }
   7 await prisma.outboxEvent.create({ ... });             // 4. DB Write

  Exploit Scenario:
   1. The Node.js process experiences an OOM kill or DB connection timeout precisely after Step 1.
   2. Result: The Expense record is created, but the outboxEvent is never written. The review queue will never notify managers. The record is effectively
      orphaned in the UI.

  [MEDIUM] 4. Missing Database Constraints (Negative Amounts)
  Vulnerability: Missing Constraints / Stuck State
  Flows: Expense Creation

  The Code Path:
  The Prisma schema defines amount_paise BigInt but has no check constraints. ExpensesService.createExpense does not validate amountPaise > 0.

  Exploit Scenario:
   1. User submits an expense with amountPaise = -50000.
   2. The expense is created, reviewed, and approved successfully (state transitions don't check amount).
   3. Finance attempts to markPaid.
   4. The LedgerService throws: Error("Total transaction amount must be greater than zero").
   5. Result: The transaction is permanently stuck in approved state. It cannot be paid, and it cannot be rejected (since state machine forbids approved ->
      rejected).

  ---

  3. PRINCIPAL REMEDIATION PLAN

  Fix 1: Unified Idempotency Domain (P0)
  Financial events must be keyed by their business aggregate, not the trigger mechanism.
  Action: Update TicketsService.ts to use the exact same idempotency key as ExpensesService.ts.

   1 // In TicketsService.ts
   2 idempotencyKey: `reimburse-ledger-${ticket.expense_id}`, // Matches ExpensesService exactly

  Fix 2: Pessimistic Locking on Aggregates (P0)
  Read operations that dictate state machine transitions must lock the aggregate root.
  Action: Refactor all state transitions to perform a SELECT ... FOR UPDATE inside the transaction before evaluating state.

    1 // Refactored State Transition Pattern
    2 await prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => {
    3   // 1. Lock the row
    4   const expense = await tx.$queryRaw`SELECT * FROM "expenses" WHERE id = ${id}::uuid FOR UPDATE`;
    5
    6   // 2. Evaluate State
    7   if (expense[0].status !== 'submitted') throw new Error("Invalid state");
    8
    9   // 3. Mutate
   10   await tx.expense.update({ ... });
   11   await tx.outboxEvent.create({ ... });
   12 });

  Fix 3: Strict Transaction Boundaries (P1)
  All related DB writes in a business workflow must be wrapped in a single transaction.
  Action: Rewrite ExpensesService.createExpense and DocumentsService.confirmUpload to wrap the create, policy evaluation, auto-approve update, and
  outboxEvent creation into a single prisma.$transaction.

  Fix 4: Database-Level Constraints (P2)
  Never trust the application layer with financial constraints.
  Action: Add raw SQL migrations to enforce invariants at the Postgres level.

   1 ALTER TABLE "expenses" ADD CONSTRAINT chk_expense_amount_positive CHECK (amount_paise > 0);
   2 ALTER TABLE "JournalEntry" ADD CONSTRAINT chk_journal_amount_positive CHECK (amount_paise > 0);

  Summary of Audit
  The @spendos/ledger engine is well-engineered and correctly prevents double-entry IF given the correct idempotency keys. The fatal flaw lies in the
  Service Layer leaking context, mismanaging idempotency keys, and failing to use pessimistic row locks for the Expense aggregate. Implementing the 4 fixes
  above will restore total financial consistency.
▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄▄
 > Act as a Senior SRE.

   Assume deployment tomorrow.

   Review:

   Docker
   CI/CD
   Secrets
   Env variables
   SSL/TLS
   Reverse proxies
   Backups
   Monitoring
   Logging

   Determine:

   Single points of failure

  SRE Review: Production Readiness Assessment:
  Acting as a Senior SRE to perform a Production Readiness Review of the SpendOS application before a hypothetical deployment.

  ✓  FindFiles  '**/Dockerfile' → No files found
  ✓  FindFiles  '**/.env*' → Found 3 matching file(s)

✦ PRODUCTION READINESS REPORT: SpendOS

  Role: Senior Site Reliability Engineer (SRE)
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target Deployment Date: Tomorrow
  Status: REJECTED (DO NOT DEPLOY)

  ---

  1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

  The SpendOS application is currently in a "Local Development" state. It lacks fundamental infrastructure-as-code, deployment automation, security
  boundaries, and operational observability. Deploying this architecture tomorrow will result in immediate operational blind spots, potential data loss
  during incidents, and severe scaling issues.

  PRODUCTION READINESS SCORE: 15 / 100

  ---

  2. INFRASTRUCTURE & DEPLOYMENT REVIEW

  2.1 Docker & Orchestration
   - Status: Missing
   - Finding: There are no production Dockerfiles in the repository. The existing docker-compose.yml is strictly for local development (runs PostgreSQL with
     password=password, Redis, and Mailhog).
   - Risk: Cannot deploy to ECS, EKS, or Kubernetes without containerizing the api and dashboard apps.

  2.2 CI/CD Pipelines
   - Status: Missing
   - Finding: No .github/workflows, GitLab CI, or Jenkins pipelines exist.
   - Risk: Manual, undocumented deployments. No automated unit testing, linting, or integration testing gate before hitting production.

  2.3 SSL/TLS & Reverse Proxies
   - Status: Missing
   - Finding: The Fastify server binds directly to 0.0.0.0:3000 over HTTP. There is no configuration for Nginx, Caddy, HAProxy, or AWS ALB for TLS
     termination.
   - Risk: Traffic is sent in plaintext. Cookie security (secure: process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production') will fail if TLS is not terminated correctly at an
     edge proxy.

  ---

  3. SECURITY & CONFIGURATION

  3.1 Secrets Management
   - Status: Critical Risk
   - Finding: Configuration relies entirely on .env files loaded at runtime. There is no integration with AWS Secrets Manager, HashiCorp Vault, or SOPS.
   - Risk: High probability of secrets leaking into source control or being mismanaged during manual deployments.

  3.2 Environment Variables
   - Status: Inadequate
   - Finding: Fallbacks are dangerous. E.g., process.env.COOKIE_SECRET || "spendos-secret-key".
   - Risk: If the production environment is misconfigured and COOKIE_SECRET is omitted, the application falls back to a publicly known string, instantly
     compromising all session cookies.

  ---

  4. RELIABILITY & ARCHITECTURE

  4.1 Single Points of Failure (SPOFs)
   - SPOF 1: API Process State (Cron & Outbox)
     - Issue: startCronJobs() and startOutboxWorker() are invoked inside the Fastify server.ts startup sequence.
     - Impact: If you horizontally scale the API to 3 pods, 3 identical Cron jobs will fire, sending duplicate SLA breach emails to clients. While the
       outbox worker uses SKIP LOCKED (safe), the node-cron scheduler has no distributed locking mechanism.
   - SPOF 2: In-Memory / Single Redis
     - Issue: Rate limiting and Pulse Dashboard cache rely on a single Redis instance connection. No Sentinel or Redis Cluster configuration.

  4.2 Backups & Disaster Recovery
   - Status: Missing
   - Finding: While the README mentions using Neon Postgres, there are no documented Point-in-Time-Recovery (PITR) RTO/RPO SLAs, and no automated fallback
     scripts if the primary database region fails.

  ---

  5. OBSERVABILITY (LOGGING & MONITORING)

  5.1 Monitoring & Alerts
   - Status: Missing Production Controls
   - Finding: Only a basic /health endpoint exists. No Prometheus metrics (e.g., HTTP latency, DB query times, Active connections). No Datadog/NewRelic APM
     agents.
   - Risk: SREs will have zero visibility into database connection pool exhaustion or memory leaks.

  5.2 Logging
   - Status: Inadequate
   - Finding: The application uses basic Fastify logging and raw console.log() / console.error() (e.g., in outbox.processor.ts).
   - Risk: Logs are unstructured text. There is no log aggregation (ELK stack, Datadog, AWS CloudWatch). Diagnosing a distributed idempotency failure will
     require SSH-ing into individual instances and reading raw stdout.

  ---

  6. SRE REMEDIATION PLAN (BLOCKERS FOR LAUNCH)

  To achieve a minimally viable production state, the following must be implemented:

   1. Decouple Background Workers (Critical)
      - Extract cron.ts and outbox.processor.ts from server.ts into a dedicated worker app. Deploy the worker as a singleton (1 replica) to prevent
        duplicate cron executions.
   2. Containerization (Critical)
      - Write multi-stage Dockerfiles for the api, dashboard, and new worker applications using node:18-alpine.
   3. Infrastructure Edge (Critical)
      - Place an ALB/Reverse Proxy in front of the API. Enforce HTTPS/TLS 1.3 termination.
   4. Remove Unsafe Fallbacks (High)
      - Remove "spendos-secret-key". The server must crash at startup (throw new Error(...)) if critical environment variables are missing.
   5. Observability Baseline (High)
      - Install structured JSON logging (pino) globally and stream to a central aggregator.
      - Add a /metrics endpoint exposing Node.js memory and event loop lag.

  Conclusion: Deploying this application tomorrow constitutes architectural negligence. The deployment MUST be postponed until the remediation plan is
  executed.

▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀▀
✦ SCALABILITY PROJECTION & CAPACITY PLAN: SpendOS

  Author: Staff Scalability Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Target: 100k User Milestone

  ---

  1. SCALABILITY MODELING

  ┌──────────────────────────┬───────────┬─────────────┬──────────────┬───────────────┐
  │ Metric                   │ 100 Users │ 1,000 Users │ 10,000 Users │ 100,000 Users │
  ├──────────────────────────┼───────────┼─────────────┼──────────────┼───────────────┤
  │ Daily Active Users (DAU) │ 20        │ 250         │ 2,000        │ 15,000        │
  │ Expenses / Month         │ 200       │ 2,500       │ 25,000       │ 250,000       │
  │ Ledger Entries / Month   │ 400       │ 5,000       │ 50,000       │ 500,000       │
  │ API Req / Second (Peak)  │ < 1       │ 5           │ 50           │ 400+          │
  │ Storage (S3) / Month     │ 400 MB    │ 5 GB        │ 50 GB        │ 500 GB        │
  │ Database Size (1 Year)   │ < 1 GB    │ 5 GB        │ 60 GB        │ 700 GB+       │
  └──────────────────────────┴───────────┴─────────────┴──────────────┴───────────────┘
  ---

  2. RESOURCE ESTIMATES (API & DB)

  ┌───────────┬──────────────────────────┬─────────────────────┬────────────────┐
  │ Milestone │ API Nodes (2 vCPU / 4GB) │ DB Tier (Postgres)  │ Redis Tier     │
  ├───────────┼──────────────────────────┼─────────────────────┼────────────────┤
  │ 100       │ 1 (Standalone)           │ Burstable (Small)   │ Shared / Local │
  │ 1,000     │ 2 (High Availability)    │ 2 vCPU / 8GB RAM    │ 1GB Managed    │
  │ 10,000    │ 4 - 6 (Horizontal)       │ 8 vCPU / 32GB RAM   │ 4GB Managed    │
  │ 100,000   │ 15 - 20 (Auto-scaled)    │ 32 vCPU / 128GB RAM │ 16GB Cluster   │
  └───────────┴──────────────────────────┴─────────────────────┴────────────────┘
  ---

  3. PREDICTED BOTTLENECKS

  3.1 Database: The Ledger Contention (Critical)
  The current Ledger design uses SELECT FOR UPDATE on Account rows.
   - At 100k Users: During "Salary/Reimbursement Day," thousands of concurrent markPaid requests will attempt to lock the same "Corporate Treasury" account
     row.
   - Result: Transaction queueing and LockWaitTimeout errors. The database will spend more time managing locks than writing data.

  3.2 API: BigInt Serialization & Event Loop (High)
  The global BigInt serializer uses recursive JSON.stringify.
   - At 100k Users: Large reports (e.g., General Ledger for a 5,000-person company) will saturate CPU cores during serialization, blocking the Node.js event
     loop and spiking P99 latencies.

  3.3 Storage: S3 Object Enumeration (Medium)
  Listing documents for high-volume users via prisma.expense.findMany({ include: { documents: true } }) will lead to massive join tables. S3 pre-signed URL
  generation (synchronous) will add 50-100ms per request.

  ---

  4. FIRST POINT OF FAILURE

  The Outbox Polling Loop.
  The current 5-second setInterval query SELECT ... FROM OutboxEvent WHERE published = false will fail first.
   - As volume hits 100k users, the number of events generated per second will exceed the processing capacity of a single polling loop.
   - The OutboxEvent table will bloat, making the SELECT query slower and slower, leading to a "Notification Lag Death Spiral."

  ---

  5. SCALABILITY ROADMAP & RECOMMENDATIONS

  5.1 Messaging & Queues (Priority P0)
   - Replace Polling with Push: Move from setInterval polling to a dedicated task queue (e.g., BullMQ with Redis).
   - Decouple Side Effects: The Outbox Worker must be a separate auto-scaling group from the API.

  5.2 Ledger Optimization (Priority P0)
   - Account Sharding: For high-volume companies, shard the "Treasury" account into multiple sub-accounts to reduce row-level lock contention.
   - Async Ledger Posting: Consider moving ledger creation to an async job after the status change, provided strict idempotency is maintained in the job
     queue.

  5.3 Caching Strategy (Priority P1)
   - Read-Models (CQRS): Stop querying the JournalEntry table for balances. Maintain a "Materialized Balance" in Redis for every Wallet and Account.
   - CDN Strategy: Use AWS CloudFront for receipt images. Use Lambda@Edge for on-the-fly image resizing (receipt thumbnails) to save bandwidth on the
     dashboard.

  5.4 Horizontal Scaling
   - Stateless API: Ensure accessToken / refreshToken remain stateless (JWT).
   - Prisma Data Proxy: Use a connection pooler (like PgBouncer or Prisma Pulse) to prevent the 20+ API nodes from exhausting the 500-1000 connection limit
     of the Postgres instance.

  5.5 Database Maintenance
   - Partitioning: Implement Table Partitioning on JournalEntry and AuditLog by created_at (monthly partitions). This prevents full table scans on
     multi-gigabyte tables.

  ---

  FINAL VERDICT: The system is "Pilot Ready" but "Enterprise Unstable." The transition from Polling to Queuing and Row-Lock Sharding must happen before
  hitting 5,000 users.

✦ APPLICATION SECURITY AUDIT (OWASP TOP 10)

  Author: Application Security Engineer
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026

  ---

  1. VULNERABILITY REGISTER

  ┌────┬────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────┬────────┐
  │ ID │ OWASP Category │ Vulnerability                               │ Severity │ Status │
  ├────┼────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────┤
  │ V1 │ A01:2021       │ Self-Approval IDOR                          │ Critical │ Open   │
  │ V2 │ A01:2021       │ Employee Data Disclosure                    │ High     │ Open   │
  │ V3 │ A01:2021       │ Path Traversal (File Existence Probe)       │ High     │ Open   │
  │ V4 │ A03:2021       │ Missing Input Validation (Negative Amounts) │ High     │ Open   │
  │ V5 │ A05:2021       │ Dangerous Fallback Secret                   │ High     │ Open   │
  │ V6 │ A04:2021       │ Insecure Password Reset Logic               │ Medium   │ Open   │
  └────┴────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────┴──────────┴────────┘
  ---

  2. DETAILED FINDINGS

  [V3] Path Traversal (File Existence Probe)
   - File: spendos-monorepo/apps/api/src/services/documents.service.ts
   - Vulnerability: Path Traversal
   - Severity: High
   - Exploit Path: Attacker calls POST /api/v1/expenses/:id/confirm-upload with a manipulated s3Key.
   - Proof of Concept:

   1   curl -X POST http://localhost:3000/api/v1/expenses/ANY_EXPENSE_ID/confirm-upload \
   2     -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
   3     -d '{
   4       "s3Key": "../../../../../../../windows/system32/config/SAM",
   5       "fileName": "test.png",
   6       "fileType": "image/png",
   7       "fileSize": 65536,
   8       "docType": "original"
   9     }'
     - If the server returns 400 File size mismatch, the file exists.
     - If the server returns 404 File not found, the file does not exist.
   - Fix: Validate that s3Key strictly starts with companies/${actor.companyId}/expenses/${id}/ and does not contain .. sequences.

  [V4] Missing Input Validation (Negative Financial Values)
   - File: spendos-monorepo/apps/api/src/services/expenses.service.ts
   - Vulnerability: Integrity/Business Logic Flaw
   - Severity: High
   - Exploit Path: Submitting a negative amount_paise during expense creation.
   - Proof of Concept:

   1   curl -X POST http://localhost:3000/api/v1/expenses \
   2     -d '{"amountPaise": -100000000, "category": "travel", "expenseDate": "2026-06-01"}'
   - Fix: Add Zod validation .positive() to all amount fields and a DB CHECK constraint amount_paise > 0.

  [V5] Dangerous Fallback Secret (Security Misconfiguration)
   - File: spendos-monorepo/apps/api/src/server.ts
   - Vulnerability: Insecure Defaults
   - Severity: High
   - Exploit Path: If an SRE forgets to set COOKIE_SECRET in production, the app uses a publicly known hardcoded string.
   - Fix:

   1   if (!process.env.COOKIE_SECRET && process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production') {
   2     throw new Error("FATAL: COOKIE_SECRET must be set in production");
   3   }

  ---

  3. OWASP TOP 10 SCORECARD

   - A01:2021-Broken Access Control: FAIL (V1, V2, V3)
   - A02:2021-Cryptographic Failures: PASS (bcrypt, JWT)
   - A03:2021-Injection: PASS (Prisma handles SQLi, though V3 is a form of path injection)
   - A04:2021-Insecure Design: FAIL (V1, V4)
   - A05:2021-Security Misconfiguration: FAIL (V5)
   - A06:2021-Vulnerable and Outdated Components: PENDING (Needs npm audit)
   - A07:2021-Identification and Authentication Failures: PASS
   - A08:2021-Software and Data Integrity Failures: FAIL (V4)
   - A09:2021-Security Logging and Monitoring Failures: FAIL (Audit logs are fire-and-forget)
   - A10:2021-Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF): PASS (No outbound HTTP clients found in domain logic)

  ---

  4. CONCLUSION

  The application has strong cryptographic hygiene but weak business logic and access control enforcement.

  The most critical issue is the Self-Approval (V1) and Information Disclosure (V2). While SQL injection and XSS appear well-mitigated by the stack
  (Prisma/React), the Path Traversal (V3) and Negative Amount (V4) vulnerabilities represent significant risks to the system's financial and operational
  integrity.

  Immediate Remediation Required: Address V1, V2, V3, and V4 before any production pilot.

✦ CTO LAUNCH RECOMMENDATION & READINESS REPORT

  Author: Chief Technology Officer (CTO)
  Date: Tuesday, 2 June 2026
  Subject: SpendOS Beta Launch Evaluation

  ---

  1. COMPONENT SCORES

  ┌───────────────────────┬──────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Domain                │ Score    │ Rationale                                                                                              │
  │                       │ (0-100)  │                                                                                                        │
  ├───────────────────────┼──────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Security Score        │ 25 / 100 │ Critical IDORs (Self-Approval, Directory Leak), Path Traversal, and unsafe fallback secrets.           │
  │ Scalability Score     │ 30 / 100 │ Outbox polling loop will fail under moderate load. Severe lock contention expected on the Ledger.      │
  │ Reliability Score     │ 35 / 100 │ Cron job SPOFs (duplicate emails if scaled), fire-and-forget audit logs.                               │
  │ Infrastructure Score  │ 10 / 100 │ No Dockerfiles, no CI/CD, no edge proxy/TLS termination. Running bare Node on port 3000.               │
  │ Financial Integrity   │ 20 / 100 │ Catastrophic double-payout vulnerability. Missing negative amount constraints. TOCTOU race conditions. │
  │ Score                 │          │                                                                                                        │
  │ Maintainability Score │ 70 / 100 │ Solid use of Turborepo, Next.js, Prisma, Zod, and Fastify. Good foundational ledger design, despite    │
  │                       │          │ service-layer coupling.                                                                                │
  └───────────────────────┴──────────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  OVERALL SHIP READINESS SCORE: 18 / 100

  ---

  2. DECISION

  [ DO NOT LAUNCH ]

  The foundational architecture (Double-Entry Ledger, Outbox Pattern) is conceptually sound and aligned with enterprise standards. However, the execution at
  the Service Layer is dangerously flawed. Launching this system in its current state will result in immediate financial loss (double-payouts), security
  breaches (IDORs), and operational failure (duplicate crons).

  ---

  3. LAUNCH BLOCKERS

  Blocker 1: Double Payout via Idempotency Key Mismatch
   - Business Impact: Direct loss of corporate funds. Double-draining the treasury account.
   - Technical Impact: The ledger records duplicate transactions for a single expense resolution.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 2 Hours (Unify idempotency keys in TicketsService and ExpensesService).

  Blocker 2: Self-Approval IDOR (Broken Dual-Control)
   - Business Impact: Fraud. Managers can submit and immediately approve their own fake expenses for payout.
   - Technical Impact: Bypasses the core value proposition of the system's compliance engine.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 1 Hour (Add if (expense.submitted_by === actor.userId) throw ForbiddenError in ExpensesService.approveExpense).

  Blocker 3: Missing Transaction Boundaries & Pessimistic Locking
   - Business Impact: Orphaned expenses, stuck states, and corrupted audit logs.
   - Technical Impact: TOCTOU race conditions during state transitions; incomplete side effects if the API crashes mid-request.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 6-8 Hours (Refactor state transitions to use SELECT FOR UPDATE inside prisma.$transaction).

  Blocker 4: Path Traversal in Document Verification
   - Business Impact: Exposure of highly sensitive corporate receipts and internal system files.
   - Technical Impact: Allows attackers to probe local filesystem or cross-tenant S3 directories via manipulated s3Key.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 1 Hour (Strict regex/prefix validation on s3Key).

  Blocker 5: Infrastructure & Cron SPOF
   - Business Impact: Extreme unprofessionalism (spamming clients with duplicate SLA emails), high risk of downtime.
   - Technical Impact: No containerization prevents horizontal scaling. Cron jobs running on API nodes will execute multiple times.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 1-2 Days (Extract workers, write Dockerfiles, configure Docker Swarm / ECS).

  Blocker 6: Negative Amount Manipulation
   - Business Impact: Artificial inflation of Treasury balances (printing fake money).
   - Technical Impact: No DB-level or application-level constraints preventing amount_paise < 0.
   - Estimated Fix Time: 2 Hours (Add Zod .positive() and DB CHECK constraints).

  ---

  4. PRIORITIZED ROADMAP

  Next 24 Hours: "Stop the Bleeding" (Financial & Security Integrity)
   1. Fix Blocker 1 & 2: Standardize idempotency keys and enforce dual-control (Self-Approval block).
   2. Fix Blocker 4 & 6: Patch the Path Traversal vulnerability and enforce amount_paise > 0.
   3. Fix Information Disclosure: Restrict GET /users so employees only see their own profile or public team info, not admin metadata.
   4. Remove Fallback Secrets: Ensure COOKIE_SECRET throws an error if missing in production.

  Next 7 Days: "Operational Baseline" (Infrastructure & Transactions)
   1. Refactor Transactions (Blocker 3): Wrap all business workflows (Create Expense, Approve, Reject) into strict prisma.$transaction blocks with
      pessimistic locking on the Expense aggregate.
   2. Infrastructure (Blocker 5): Containerize the API and Dashboard. Setup basic CI/CD (GitHub Actions) for build and test validation.
   3. Extract Workers: Move startCronJobs and startOutboxWorker out of the API layer into a standalone worker service.
   4. Audit Log Integrity: Move AuditService.log into the ACID transaction boundary.

  Next 30 Days: "Scale to 10k Users"
   1. Replace Polling with Queues: Swap the 5-second SQL Outbox polling loop for a robust Redis-backed queue (BullMQ).
   2. Event-Driven Coupling: Implement an internal Event Emitter to decouple ExpensesService from NotificationsService.
   3. Observability: Implement structured JSON logging (Pino) and a centralized APM (Datadog/NewRelic) for metrics and tracing.
   4. BigInt Serialization: Replace the recursive JSON.stringify with a performant custom serializer to prevent event-loop blocking.

  Next 90 Days: "Enterprise Maturity" (100k+ Users)
   1. Ledger Sharding: Implement Treasury account sharding to alleviate SELECT FOR UPDATE lock contention during peak payout days.
   2. Read-Models / CQRS: Implement Redis caching for Wallet balances and general ledger rollups to remove read pressure from Postgres.
   3. S3 Pre-signed URL Hardening: Add Content-Length and strict MIME-type enforcement at the AWS IAM/Policy level for uploads.
   4. Database Partitioning: Partition JournalEntry and AuditLog tables by month to ensure long-term query performance.
